Subject: [PLUG] software for automatic network diagrams?
In-Reply-To: <200807191550.02560.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
References: <867ibhd2fl.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
	<200807191550.02560.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
Message-ID: <86k5fhaypb.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

>>>>> "Eric" == Eric Wilhelm <scratchcomputing at gmail.com> writes:

Russell> [...] but I'm looking for something that works from a
Russell> "source" file rather than lots and lots of little mouse
Russell> clicks and drags and stuff.

Eric> Graphviz (aka dot).

Eric>   digraph "my network" { node1 -> switch1; node2 -> switch1;
Eric> switch1 -> switch2; node3 -> switch2; node4 -> switch2; }

Eric> It then does the node layout automatically.  You can group
Eric> things with a subgraph{} and influence the placement by ordering
Eric> or add explicit placement by coordinates.

Eric> It may not be well-suited to creating small tidy diagrams, but
Eric> it works great for mapping large quantities of connections.

I'm particularly interested in something that labels interfaces with
CIDR notation, and yeah, I'm looking for small tidy diagrams (at least
in cases of small tidy-ish networks).  I am familiar with graphviz,
and I'd be fine with something it generated so long as I can get
decent labelling on the interfaces.

Larry's netmap seems to be a traceroute-driven thing.  I can supply
the network interface information, I just want something to draw the
tidy graphs with labelling.  The other one Larry pointed at looks not
like what I'm looking for.

Thanks for the input.


-- 
Russell Senior, Secretary
russell at personaltelco.net

a stock version.  Easy to fix with the original being saved as 
named.conf.rpmsave

znmeb at cesmail.net wrote:
> Quoting Russell Senior <russell at personaltelco.net>:
>
>   
>> I am looking for existing FOSS software that can take a description of
>> a network and convert it into a nice graphic.  I know I can use
>> various tools to draw my own network diagram, but I'm looking for
>> something that works from a "source" file rather than lots and lots of
>> little mouse clicks and drags and stuff.
>>
>> Any suggestions?
>>     
>
> I think the easiest thing would be to load dia, make a sample diagram  
> with one of every gizmo you've got on your network, then save it as an  
> XML file. Then you can "just" open it up in an XML editor and cut and  
> paste away.
>
> If this is *your* network, you might be able to find some "network  
> discovery" tools that would automate a bit more of the process. But if  
> you're actually looking to code something, you'd probably find it  
> easier to use dia to get you started.
>
> Dia is scriptable, but I don't remember what the scripting language  
> is. It's either Python or Guile, which is a Scheme dialect.
>   
>>     
Zenoss (www.zenoss.org) is the tool you want, auto-discovery plus 
configurable devices, plus I think it will import configs (not sure 
about that). As long as you have the snmp read community string, you 
should be able to just map the whole thing. This is a full blow network 
monitoring and management tool.

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Sun Jul 20 09:31:45 2008
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Sun, 20 Jul 2008 09:31:45 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] software for automatic network diagrams?
In-Reply-To: <86k5fhaypb.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <867ibhd2fl.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
	<200807191550.02560.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
	<86k5fhaypb.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <200807200931.45549.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from Russell Senior
# on Saturday 19 July 2008 22:53:

>I'm particularly interested in something that labels interfaces with
>CIDR notation, and yeah, I'm looking for small tidy diagrams (at least
>in cases of small tidy-ish networks). ?I am familiar with graphviz,
>and I'd be fine with something it generated so long as I can get
>decent labelling on the interfaces.

The label can be whatever you want (though you may have to use an 
explicit label instead of the implicit label derived from the node 
name.)  If you use the 'record' node type, you can even have something 
like:

  -------------------------------
  |          platypus           |
  -------------------------------
  | 192.168.0.10 | 192.168.0.11 |
  -------------------------------

Where connections can point to any of the three parts of that node.

  platypus [
   label="{<_>platypus|{{<ip1>192.168.0.10}|{<ip2>192.168.0.11}}}",
   shape=record
  ];
  foo -> platypus;
  platypus:ip1 -> bar;
  platypus:ip2 -> baz;

Assuming this is what you meant anyway...  If you meant something else, 
the answer is maybe different, but probably still yes WRT graphviz.

--Eric

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Sun Jul 20 13:50:35 2008
From: znmeb at cesmail.net (M. Edward (Ed) Borasky)
Date: Sun, 20 Jul 2008 13:50:35 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Email, Comcast, Links, etc.(sigh)
Message-ID: <1216587035.5626.42.camel@DreamScape>

It has been quite an interesting few hours. Some time on Friday, I
discovered that my emails weren't going anywhere. After discovering
yesterday that I could send from my SpamCop webmail account, I went to
the Comcast web site. I tried sending some emails from there, and that
didn't work either.

So I got the Comcast Live Chat person. He checked a few things, but he
couldn't figure out what was happening either. He asked me to try
changing my password, then told me that the server was down. So ...
still no luck.

Today after a couple of hours, I figured out what the problem was. My
signature had two links in it. By a process of elimination, it became
apparent that Comcast was blocking all the emails that had my blog link
in the signature. I haven't tried it with the link in the text of the
emails yet. In any event, if you are reading this email, I have
succeeded.

So ... Comcast blocks some links but not others? How did my blog get on
a blacklist? Why isn't it smart enough to recognize a link without
"http://" in it?

Oh, yeah ... more Comcast goodies ... if you try to access their site
with Seamonkey, it tells you it's time you upgraded your browser. ;)
-- 
M. Edward (Ed) Borasky
ruby-perspectives.blogspot.com

Please show your support and give a warm welcome to Andrew Harris, the
15 year old that I was able to coax into giving a talk this year at
Ubuntu Live, that was eventually moved to OSCON due to cancellation
:-)
http://en.oreilly.com/oscon2008/public/schedule/detail/2674

"""
Teenbuntu: Reaching Out to Teens
Andrew Harris (Teens on Linux.org)
4:30pm Thursday, 07/24/2008
People, Ubuntu
Location: D135

This talk is given by Andrew "Tuna" Harris, the teenaged founder of
TeensOnLinux.org, and Samuel Baldwin, a 15-year-old hacker from
Boston. It will focus on three main points: why we should get teens
involved in open source, getting them interested, and making freedom
in software matter to them.

Teens are a great market for open source. They love community and the
"breaking away from the Man" sort of feeling, so they are quick to
adopt alternatives to what everyone else uses (take that society!). As
students, they usually aren't too busy to find some time to contribute
something. It is also the age of learning and exploration of new
ideas. Getting involved in Ubuntu and FOSS is a great way to learn
something new.

Many people say that Linux is a horrible platform for gaming, and for
that reason, nobody but old Unix hackers with chest-length beards ever
use it. However, with the development of tools like Wine and
CrossOver, along with awesome games like Tremulous and OpenArena, that
is becoming less and less true. Benchmark tests have shown that many
games, such as World of Warcraft, actually run better on Linux using
Wine than it does on Windows.

Teens also use Windows for things like instant messaging and music.
Pidgin and Mugshot's desktop integration make Ubuntu the ultimate OS
for such purposes. Pidgin has become probably the best instant
messaging client freely available on the Internet, with support for
more protocols than any one person would ever use in their entire
life. Users of Yahoo!, AIM, and even MSN will feel right at home with
Pidgin. Amarok and Rythmbox both have Magnatune integration that is
comparable to Apple's iTunes music store. You can listen to the songs
directly from the player and buy albums just as you would with iTunes
or Napster. The difference is that the music is DRM-free and licensed
so that you are allowed to share the music you buy with a friend!

I believe that teens could be a great and welcome addition to the
Ubuntu community. Their ideas could push us into the mainstream and
beyond.
"""

"""
Andrew Harris
Teens on Linux.org

Andrew "Tuna" Harris is a 15 year old living in Arizona. He founded
TeensOnLinux.org in the summer of 2007. His interests include
programming, tea, heavy metal, European techno, and Open Source. Tuna
likes to program in Ruby and Gambas, and prefers Earl Grey tea. Tuna
has been using Ubuntu since his laptop refused to boot Windows about a
year and a half ago. Ronnie Tucker of Full Circle Magazine recommended
Kubuntu Dapper to him, and has been happily running the 'buntu's
since.
"""

Kristian Erik Hermansen

http://kristian-hermansen.com

Ubuntu. I tried opening the same .docx file with OOo 2.4 on Windows
without any luck.  I haven't dug deep enough to figure out what magic
Ubuntu is doing.

Adapter: PCI adapter
Core0 Temp:
             +74?C

w83697hf-isa-0290
Adapter: ISA adapter
VCore:     +1.52 V  (min =  +0.05 V, max =  +0.02 V)       ALARM
+3.3V:     +3.22 V  (min =  +2.83 V, max =  +1.86 V)       ALARM
+5V:       +4.92 V  (min =  +0.05 V, max =  +0.46 V)       ALARM

-12V:      -0.35 V  (min =  -0.44 V, max =  +0.88 V)

fan1:        0 RPM  (min =   82 RPM, div = 128)              ALARM
fan2:     3947 RPM  (min = 3994 RPM, div = 2)              ALARM
temp1:       +40?C  (high =   +32?C, hyst =   +22?C)   sensor = thermistor   ALARM
temp2:     +66.5?C  (high =   +80?C, hyst =   +75?C)   sensor = thermistor      
alarms:   Chassis intrusion detection                      ALARM
beep_enable:
          Sound alarm enabled

Sometimes fans that are not 3-wire give a spurious reading of 0RPM. Other than that, 74C is pretty hot. I understand that sometimes this program gives spurious results with amd64 architecture, but should I be concerned with these results?

On Sun, Jul 20, 2008 at 07:28:44AM -0700, Michael Rasmussen wrote:
MR> You don't mention when this problem started.
MR> Is this the only domain you cannot resolve internally?

Earlier I would have said "only dwstudios and hostica".  However, today,
an email to Aaron Baer also choked, so add slyness.org (64.122.12.110)
to the trouble list.  I don't know when the problem started, but the
problem rate suggests it occured with the recent DNS changes.

Another change that occured in the last two months was the change
to Verizon FIOS and the addition of an Actiontec cable modem + 
router + etc.  That does a lot more than the old Linksys cable 
modem that I used for Comcast - among other things, it can act as a
firewall, and adds another layer of NAT - so it may be part of the
problem.

Note that a laptop connected directly to the Actiontec, using DHCP
and the Actiontec+Verizon as the domain name server, will resolve all
the problematic URLs.

MR> Have you checked your firewall logs?

I have most of the rules set to DROP, so not much gets logged.  However,
I can turn the firewall off (yikes!) and see the same problem.

MR> The recent DNS systems patch flurry was to ensure source port randomization. 

I couldn't find a simple explanation of source port randomization, in
operational terms.  How does that affect operation?

MR> Side issue:
MR> Has your package management system upgraded your bind installation?  Fedora, 
MR> CentOS and derivatives had a problem with the named.conf being replaced with 
MR> a stock version.  Easy to fix with the original being saved as 
MR> named.conf.rpmsave

The package management system upgraded named, but not /etc/named.conf (which
actually simlinks to the chroot version of the file).

---

I just figured out that the named log files are now going into
/var/named/chroot/var/log/named/  ;  I wasn't seeing them at first,
but now I can see that all sorts of good stuff is getting logged.

So now I have a wealth of detail to learn from.  I think that (plus
the BIND documentation, which I will slog through)  will give me a
hint.  I have a 15yo O'Reilly book on Bind and DNS, which seems to
be uselessly obsolete, but the online stuff may yield some understanding.

Keith

----------------------------------------------------------------------------
To the list, don't forget to add the DNS 1.0.0.0 problem.

For me, oddly, it has only manifested with "www" hostnames. In other
words, I get 1.0.0.0 for "www.bob.com" but I get a good IP for
bob.com.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
I used to have very frequent DNS 1.0.0.0 problems. For me at least,
the solution was to put the ISP DNS host IP addresses in the NIC IP
settings (static DNS) on the computer to which the Actiontec is
connected via ethernet. If the DNS info is left as dynamic, I am
guaranteed to see frequent 1.0.0.0 errors. Qwest DSL support was no
help in figuring this out. They had never heard of the 1.0.0.0
problem.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------


Ali

> Sometimes fans that are not 3-wire give a spurious reading of 0RPM.
> Other than that, 74C is pretty hot. I understand that sometimes this

>  Robert "Tim" Kopp 
> http://analytic.tripod.com/

Okay, a disclaimer right off the bat.  I don't know squat about that
particular motherboard, so this is all speculation on my part.  Take
my advice with a grain of salt, or perhaps the entire salt cellar.  :-)

Are you sure you've got the right driver for that motherboard?  The
limits shown look really screwy.  If the power supply was actually
putting out what the limits imply, then your computer wouldn't work at
all. The actual readings don't look too far off, except maybe the
negative supply voltages.  Try rebooting, and checking to see what the
BIOS sees.  (Most of the BIOS programs that I've seen display the sensor
readings somewhere or another.)  That will tell you what the readings
really are.  Then you can compare with what lm-sensors is telling you.  

Okay, I've just googled lm-sensors av8 abit and found this page:
  <http://www.lm-sensors.org/wiki/Configurations/Abit/AV8>
It's an example configuration file for the AV8 mobo.  Maybe that will help?

Dale

I haven't used mdbtools in a while (a year or so?).  IIRC, you may
need to be careful with embedded end-of-line characters when you dump
to a text file.  Also, I have a vague memory of where clauses not
being honored.  That is, you can write "... where foo=10", but it will
simply ignore it.

But other than a few quirks which had some easy workarounds and may be
fixed by now, the mdbtools worked great for my needs.

Good luck and let us know how it works for you.

- Robert

Carlos Konstanski <ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com> dijo:

> > cannot offer any help.
> >

> 
> Yep, you were.
> 
> I've been messing with it more, and it seems that a lot of the tools act
> directly on the .mdb file.  I may not need an ODBC config at all.  I'm
> considering going the route of exporting the data into a text file dump, and
> then importing it into a more usable database.  This seems to be quite doable
> with the basic tools.

Carlos,

I recently needed to read an MS Access database file. Actually, all I
needed was one table. After much messing around I finally discovered
that Kexi can read MS Access database files. Since I wanted to get it
into open source format, I just let Kexi import it into its native
SQLite format. 

Eventually I discovered that Kexi and SQLite are not quite ready for
prime time. Too many features not yet implemented. So I connected
OpenOffice Base the the Kexi file. I thought that would solve the
problem of the missing features, but it turns out that OOo Base simply
reads the external data and uses the features of the external program.
If the external program cannot handle a particular query, then the same
query in OOo will fail as well. And when I say missing features I'm
talking some really basic stuff, like being able to append records to a
table.

In the end I moved it into OOo Base native format where I had no
problems with missing features. Unfortunately, that was not a perfect
solution either, as OOo Base is Java and the screen refresh is slower
than the second coming.

In a huge stroke of luck, I discovered that my Access tables are all
actually "Linked ODBC" objects.  They are all database links to an
MSSQL 2000 server's tables.  So I'm off the hook for this go-around,
since it will be much better to deal with a real database that has a
network address and stuff.

There are quite a few Access databases floating around in my
department, all performing scarily critical tasks, so I'm still
interested in this suite of utilities.  Keep the tips coming!  I found
the various mdb-* commands to work as advertised.  The Linked ODBC
tables were not visible, however.  I guess it can only read the data
that is actually contained in the .mdb file.

Carlos

> 4GB address space, but separate processes can be assigned their own  4GB
> space.

I found this link which suggests there might be a problem with the
version of Grub that comes with Debian:

http://howtoforge.org/make-your-xen-pae-kernel-work-with-more-than-4gb-ram-debian-etch-grub

Using PAE your processes still only have 32-bit address spaces, so yes
you can only address 4GB for a single process.

Just a reminder.

O'Reilly's OSCON (OpenSource Conference) is in Portland at the Oregon
Convention Center this week.  See
http://en.oreilly.com/oscon2008/public/content/home for details.  The
best days of the conference are Wednesday and Thursday.  The
conference is expensive, but there are many fun free things for people
who can not afford the conference fees.  O'Reilly is very good
committed to Open Source and realize that many Open Source people have
limited resources.  As a result, O'Reilly let's everyone into the Expo
and the Birds of the Feather sessions and the OSCAMP room for free.
Also, there are many interesting conversations going on a the halls
and everyone can get to these.

Finally, PLUG has a booth in the Expo.  John Jason Jordan
<johnxj at comcast.net> is organizing this and I'm sure he could use some
help.  PLUG signed up for this booth, but people from other local Open
Source and Linux groups are welcome to share it and certainly welcome
to have us pass out your group's flyers.

> to Verizon FIOS and the addition of an Actiontec cable modem +
> router + etc.  That does a lot more than the old Linksys cable

> firewall, and adds another layer of NAT - so it may be part of the
> problem.

On Tue, Jul 22, 2008 at 2:30 PM, Ali Corbin <ali.corbin at gmail.com> wrote:
> > This sounds suspiciously familiar.  I sometimes have sporadic dns
> > resolution problems.
> > I've found that I can fix them by cycling power on my cable modem.
> > I'm not at home right now, so I can't be sure, but I think mine is
> > also an Actiontec.
> > Ali
> >

On Tue, Jul 22, 2008 at 02:42:27PM -0700, Ali Corbin wrote:
> I googled around for a bit, and found, at
>     http://www.broadbandreports.com/forum/remark,11430965
> 
> ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
> To the list, don't forget to add the DNS 1.0.0.0 problem.
> 
> For me, oddly, it has only manifested with "www" hostnames. In other
> words, I get 1.0.0.0 for "www.bob.com" but I get a good IP for
> bob.com.
> ----------------------------------------------------------------------------
> I used to have very frequent DNS 1.0.0.0 problems. For me at least,
> the solution was to put the ISP DNS host IP addresses in the NIC IP
> settings (static DNS) on the computer to which the Actiontec is
> connected via ethernet. If the DNS info is left as dynamic, I am
> guaranteed to see frequent 1.0.0.0 errors. Qwest DSL support was no
> help in figuring this out. They had never heard of the 1.0.0.0
> problem.
> -------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Interesting pointer, but that does not seem to be my problem - I am
running my own domain server, not an outside one, and I am starting
with "hints" from the root name servers.  The problem is that some
of the DNS requests do not appear to get answered.

I found this:
   http://aplawrence.com/MacOSX/dns_puzzle.html

And that may be a fruitful path to explore.  The author says that
the Actiontec is truncating UDP packets longer than 512 bytes,
which can cause a fallback to TCP.  However, some DNS servers do
not support DNS queries on TCP.  More experimentation needed.
The author points at:

http://www.dslreports.com/forum/r17679150-Howto-make-ActionTec-MI424WR-a-network-bridge

Which is how to turn the Actiontec into a bridge.  Personally, I 
would rather get rid of the damned thing entirely and connect through
the CAT5 that I ran to the other side of the wall from the ONT.
That way I will not be burning power in it.

Alternately, I will learn how to configure named.conf so DNS
pulls name service from my offsite server for outside addresses.
Or something ...

Keith

In my experience, removing the ActionTec router from the equation is  
fully supported by Verizon. Just unplug it and connect whatever router  
you wish to use instead to the ethernet jack previously occupied by  
the ActionTec router.

When I've supervised their install teams in the past I've asked if  
their router is required, and the answer I got every time was no. On  
one occasion I said we don't want to use it, this Linux pc is going  
straight into the wall, and the technician said okay. He said they  
have to leave the router on site, just stick it in the closet or  
something.

Depends on the installer probably.  We just had it installed this past
weekend and the installer *insisted* on using the MoCA (coax)
connection instead of Ethernet.  He was very nice and professional and
did a great job installing everything, so I didn't argue too much (I
also didn't really care).  It works so far and had the added benefit
of using an existing coax cable and thus didn't involve any new holes
through my swiss cheese walls.

I haven't noticed any DNS weirdness yet, but I'll keep an eye on it.
The router definitely runs it's own DNS server, I suppose for caching
and to provide the ".home" name resolution locally:

From galens at seitzassoc.com  Wed Jul 23 08:42:34 2008
From: galens at seitzassoc.com (Galen Seitz)

Guy Letourneau wrote:
> I am running Ubuntu HH.
> 
> The desktop includes a trash / wastebasket application.
> Problem is I dropped a directory in ther and it won't Empty.
> 
> I'd like to hit it with 'sudo' rmdir.
> 
> Where are trash files stored in Ubuntu?

~/.local/share/Trash/files on my machine, but I'm running Xubuntu. 
You should be able to find your trash directory the same way I did. 
Put a file with a unique name into the trash and then search for it 
using find.

touch Desktop/xyzzy.junk
drag xyzzy.junk into the trash
find ~ -name xyzzy.junk

> 
> Also, a command line question: I tried seaching for the directory name 
> using ls -R but I found that '-R' didn't search recursively (doesn't 
> 'recursive' mean 'search all the subdirectories too?') I tested this on 
> a file I knew was in /home/[...]/tmp/swapby searching from '/' and it 
> didn't find it.

-R is the correct option, but you probably want -a as well in order to 
get dot files.  As per the above, find is probably a better choice for 
what you are wanting to do.

galen

Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0807230842540.9208@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Wed, 23 Jul 2008, John Jason Jordan wrote:

> Pardon me, I did not make myself clear. I meant that Kexi and *Kexi's
> implementation of SQLite* are not ready for prime time.

   Ah! You're pardoned.

> It's been a while, but several standard queries were not yet implemented
> in Kexi. It's possible that they could be done with SQLite without the
> Kexi front end.

   What's a 'standard query?' Just curious because I've not encountered such
a term. Would 'standard' be application-specific?

> I am not an SQL guru, hence I need a graphical front end.

   John, this is a common misconception that has led to all sorts of errors.
Some are insignificant, others (such as the engineers in the space program
not standardizing on a measurement system) much more expensive and
significant by any measure. Example: when Lotus-1,2,3 came out it had a menu
item for 'Variance' and another for 'Standard Deviation.' That's fine,
except the coders who wrote Lotus-1,2,3 were not statisticians and they used
the population formula rather than the sample formula. The latter asssumes
that you have measurements for every individual in the population. Rarely,
if ever in the real world, is that the case. Ergo, every answer was slightly
wrong. Knowing how to use the statistical functions of the spreadsheet did
not guarantee that they were used correctly.

   The analogy I've used for years when discussing this issue is that
teaching someone how to use a word processor does not make her a writer.

   In your situation, not knowing SQL means that you need to trust whoever
wrote the GUI front end to an application to really know what it is you want
or need as a result to a query. If the work you are doing is important, then
it behooves you to know what's going on behind the curtain. Only when we are
confident that we know what we're doing can we apply an automated tool.

Rich

> > I am not an SQL guru, hence I need a graphical front end.
> 
>    John, this is a common misconception that has led to all sorts of errors.
> Some are insignificant, others (such as the engineers in the space program
> not standardizing on a measurement system) much more expensive and
> significant by any measure. Example: when Lotus-1,2,3 came out it had a menu
> item for 'Variance' and another for 'Standard Deviation.' That's fine,
> except the coders who wrote Lotus-1,2,3 were not statisticians and they used
> the population formula rather than the sample formula. The latter asssumes
> that you have measurements for every individual in the population. Rarely,
> if ever in the real world, is that the case. Ergo, every answer was slightly
> wrong. Knowing how to use the statistical functions of the spreadsheet did
> not guarantee that they were used correctly.
> 
>    The analogy I've used for years when discussing this issue is that
> teaching someone how to use a word processor does not make her a writer.
> 
>    In your situation, not knowing SQL means that you need to trust whoever
> wrote the GUI front end to an application to really know what it is you want
> or need as a result to a query. If the work you are doing is important, then
> it behooves you to know what's going on behind the curtain. Only when we are
> confident that we know what we're doing can we apply an automated tool.

Again, let me rephrase. By "standard" I meant "ordinary" or "commonly
used." One example that I recall is that I was unable to append records
to a table. 

As for knowing what's going on behind the curtain, both Kexi and OOo
Base allow me to see the SQL code that the GUI generates. It just takes
a mouse click. Understanding the code is another matter. But I do
occasionally look at the code either because I want to learn SQL
(slowly, in my own way), or because something doesn't work as expected
and I am hoping that viewing the code will shed some light on the
matter. And in either program I can write code manually or manually
edit the code created by the GUI. 

When it comes to worrying about messing things up, I create backups
before trying something I'm not sure of. I also know tricks like
creating a delete query first as a select query. In all the years I
have used Paradox, Access and now OSS, I have yet to lose data due to
my lack of knowledge of what is going on behind the curtain.

funny, i had a much much easier time making the linux client connect
than the windows client.  the windows client was, in fact, unable to
connect, because our VPN server (also cisco) lacked any kind of modern
crypto license and the linux client could be forced back to the legacy
stuff but the windows one had no such knob to adjust.
for once i was happy that we were paying so much for a cisco support contract..

if you have a cisco vpn server and can enable/read the logging (i can
remember how to do this at the office tomorrow if you need) then i may
be able to offer some pointers.  the logging on the client was next to
useless, but the server log was obliquely informative, at least.

OS X, and Solaris.  But I have run into some quirks.  For example:

How do I drop a column?
How do I rename a column?
How do I change the column definition, e.g. text to integer?

I don't see anything obvious in the docs:

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Thu Jul 24 06:54:36 2008
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)

Subject: [PLUG] SQLite (was: mdbtools)
In-Reply-To: <4145b6790807240634o2325546en61a4b485b7d5fd86@mail.gmail.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0807221041120.4088@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0807221007190.1929@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

	<20080722195429.47393888.johnxj@comcast.net>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0807230617190.9208@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<4145b6790807240634o2325546en61a4b485b7d5fd86@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0807240648460.18828@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Thu, 24 Jul 2008, Robert Citek wrote:

> sqlite's a great little RDBMS that is portable across Windows, Linux, OS
> X, and Solaris.  But I have run into some quirks.  For example:
>
> How do I drop a column?
> How do I rename a column?

Robert,

   It's not possible now with the implementation of the ALTER TABLE command.
I believe that's on the to-do list of the developers.

> How do I change the column definition, e.g. text to integer?

   Usually by changing the data type in there. Take a look at
<http://www.sqlite.org/datatype3.html>. Text values are quoted (single or
double) while integer values are not. If I had to make those changes I'd
dump the table and use a text editor to remove the quotation marks around
the values I wanted to change. Then, drop the original table and read the
revised one.

Rich

On Thu, Jul 24, 2008 at 6:54 AM, Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> wrote:
> On Thu, 24 Jul 2008, Robert Citek wrote:
>
>> sqlite's a great little RDBMS that is portable across Windows, Linux, OS
>> X, and Solaris.  But I have run into some quirks.  For example:
>>
>> How do I drop a column?
>> How do I rename a column?
>
> Robert,
>
>   It's not possible now with the implementation of the ALTER TABLE command.
> I believe that's on the to-do list of the developers.

My current workaround is to create a new table reflecting the change
in a select statement, drop the old table, rename the new table, and
rebuild any indexes.

Is there an easier way?

>> How do I change the column definition, e.g. text to integer?
>
>   Usually by changing the data type in there. Take a look at
> <http://www.sqlite.org/datatype3.html>. Text values are quoted (single or
> double) while integer values are not. If I had to make those changes I'd
> dump the table and use a text editor to remove the quotation marks around
> the values I wanted to change. Then, drop the original table and read the
> revised one.

Which is similar to my current workaround of creating a new column
with my desired datatype, transferring the data (i.e. update), and
then do the above steps to get rid of the old column.

Again, is there an easier way?

Regards,
- Robert

Robert Citek wrote:
> How do I change the column definition, e.g. text to integer?

First ask yourself "is it necessary?"  SQLite does not enforce types.  You can
store a string or a blob in a INT column.

See http://www.sqlite.org/datatype3.html#affinity  for the background.

So the easy way is to stuff integers into your text columns.

-- 
     Michael Rasmussen
 Be Appropriate && Follow Your Curiosity

Subject: [PLUG] SQLite (was: mdbtools)
In-Reply-To: <27727.170.135.241.46.1217022806.squirrel@mail.jamhome.us>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0807221041120.4088@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0807221007190.1929@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0807230617190.9208@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<4145b6790807240634o2325546en61a4b485b7d5fd86@mail.gmail.com>
	<27727.170.135.241.46.1217022806.squirrel@mail.jamhome.us>
Message-ID: <4145b6790807252122y7d0bf990k5e09bd9b4322c156@mail.gmail.com>

On Fri, Jul 25, 2008 at 2:53 PM, Michael <michael at jamhome.us> wrote:
> Robert Citek wrote:
>> How do I change the column definition, e.g. text to integer?
>
> First ask yourself "is it necessary?"  SQLite does not enforce types.  You can
> store a string or a blob in a INT column.
>
> See http://www.sqlite.org/datatype3.html#affinity  for the background.
>
> So the easy way is to stuff integers into your text columns.

I'm interested because I want to avoid simple errors.  For example:

$ sqlite3 tmp.db .dump
BEGIN TRANSACTION;
CREATE TABLE bar (foo text);
INSERT INTO "bar" VALUES('a');
INSERT INTO "bar" VALUES('b');
INSERT INTO "bar" VALUES('c');
INSERT INTO "bar" VALUES('8');
INSERT INTO "bar" VALUES('9');
INSERT INTO "bar" VALUES('10');
COMMIT;

$ sqlite3 tmp.db 'select foo from bar ;'
a
b
c
8
9
10

$ sqlite3 tmp.db 'delete from bar where foo in ("a","b","c") ;'

$ sqlite3 tmp.db 'select foo from bar ;'
8
9
10

$ sqlite3 tmp.db 'select foo from bar where foo > 7 ;'
8
9

$ sqlite3 tmp.db 'select foo from bar where +foo > 7 ;'
8
9
10

Now that the column contains only numbers, I would like the affinity
to be integer.  My current solution:

$ sqlite3 tmp.db '
create view vbar as select +foo as "foo" from bar ;
create table bar2 as select foo from vbar ;
drop table bar;
drop view vbar;
alter table bar2 rename to bar ;
'

$ sqlite3 tmp.db 'select foo from bar where foo > 7 ;'
8
9
10

$ sqlite3 tmp.db .dump
BEGIN TRANSACTION;
CREATE TABLE 'bar'(foo);
INSERT INTO "bar" VALUES('8');
INSERT INTO "bar" VALUES('9');
INSERT INTO "bar" VALUES('10');
COMMIT;

Perhaps the best solution is to not assign any affinity at the outset.

Regards,
- Robert

It was a blast!

Because of OSCON I got to hear Mark Shuttleworth in person, and because
of Keith I got a front row center seat.

I also got t-shirts, a free book on SQLite, and numerous other swag
things. 

I am still recovering from the open bar parties hosted by O'Reilly,
Google and Sourceforge.

I met tons of people involved in OSS, Linux and other stuff we hold
dear.

I printed 200 PLUG flyers and have a little over a hundred left, plus a
lot of people passing by our booth took just a PLUG business card. I am
confident this will result in new blood for PLUG. We even had visitors
from "PLUG" - that is, the Punai, India Linux User Group. They took
copies of our stuff to take back with them. We also answered a lot of
Clinic type questions, gave geographic directions to visitors from out
of town, and even suggested how to find a tech job in Portland to
several out of towners who fell in love with Portland during OSCON.

My heartfelt thanks to Dave for arranging the booth, and to Keith and
many others who helped man it!

And, while I was only able to spend 15 minutes there, and those after
the exhibit hall closed yesterday, I was in time to meet in person Vik
Oliver of the RepRap project,
http://www.reprap.org/bin/view/Main/WebHome , a fellow from New Zealand

RepRap takes the idea of Open Source to the hardware level. Much work
still to be done, but progress on self replicating hardware is being made.

If you visit http://blog.reprap.org/ and scroll down to the entries for
Tuesday of this week, you'll see how baggage handlers mangled the
machine. When I got to the gathering area across from Powell's tables in
the lobby, the machine was up and running, having just completed a small
part.

        DefaultDepth     24
        SubSection "Display"
                Viewport   0 0
                Depth     24
        EndSubSection
EndSection

If there's another way to get more info about this, please let me know 
as I don't have a good grip on all the various Linux commands that real 
SysAdmins know.

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Sat Jul 26 11:33:57 2008
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sat, 26 Jul 2008 12:33:57 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] Logout Problem in Text Mode
In-Reply-To: <488B6801.9010106@gisnet.com>
References: <4889FDB1.60009@gisnet.com>
	<1217057604.4114.62.camel@localhost.localdomain>

Message-ID: <18571.28181.583333.368789@sphinktop.pippiandcarlos.com>

Bill Thoen writes:
 > lspci came up with:
 > 01:05.0 VGA compatible controller: ATI Technologies Inc RC410 [Radeon 
 > Xpress 200]
 > 
 > lsmod didn't show anything related to video.
 > 
 > Is this enough information for figuring out why the terminal hangs when 
 > I logout?

I use the fglrx driver with my ATI card.  I have used the radeon
friver in the past, but that was a long time ago.  I cannot remember
if the radeon driver shows up in lsmod or not.

But we're getting ahead of ourselves here.  If you are in runlevel 3
(i.e. not starting X), then it does not matter what is in your
xorg.conf file, Xorg.0.log file, or lsmod output.

Are you setting your VGA console to a non-default size?  Are you
passing something like "vga=791" as a kernel parameter in menu.lst?
This is probably not the case, or your problem would be worse - no
video at all, ever, once the kernel loads.

Are you using a non-default console font, or a non-default console
encoding?

My laptop has an especially crappy ATI Mobility card:

  01:00.0 VGA compatible controller: ATI Technologies Inc RV350 [Mobility Radeon 9600 M10]

Once I start X, I cannot switch to a VGA console, or even log out of a
console X session.  If I do, the whole display crashes in a brilliant
pattern of colors.  There is no rescue from this other than rebooting.
The keyboard still works, so I can still "reboot blind".  I mention
this to point out that certain ATI cards are prone to fatal crashes.
Of course, my issue may be with the fglrx driver, whose code only runs
from X.

Try "rebooting blind" to see if your keyboard is still responsive.
after you log out, the shell should return to a login prompt.  Login
as root blind.  Then type "reboot" blind.  Does the machine reboot?
-- 
Carlos


From gently at gmail.com  Sat Jul 26 12:00:02 2008
From: gently at gmail.com (chris (fool) mccraw)

	<18571.28181.583333.368789@sphinktop.pippiandcarlos.com>
Message-ID: <ae2db4620807261200s49631579q5e72b6114d2cc4ba@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/26/08, Carlos Konstanski <ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com> wrote:

>  But we're getting ahead of ourselves here.  If you are in runlevel 3
>  (i.e. not starting X), then it does not matter what is in your
>  xorg.conf file, Xorg.0.log file, or lsmod output.

agreed.  i think this has nothing to do with vga drivers, unless, as
Carlos wonders below, you do something weird with your console.

>  Are you setting your VGA console to a non-default size?  Are you
>  passing something like "vga=791" as a kernel parameter in menu.lst?
>  This is probably not the case, or your problem would be worse - no
>  video at all, ever, once the kernel loads.
>
>  Are you using a non-default console font, or a non-default console
>  encoding?

what i'd do is login on another virtual terminal or via ssh, and see
what is still running on the tty, if anything.  my guess is that
there's a process still running there, and that once it goes away, you
will get your login prompt back.  'ps auxw' has a 'TTY' column that
will tell you this.  the terminal you start on will be tty1.

assuming that turns up nothing, perhaps you don't have getty set up to
respawn when you logout?  what is running on the tty's you haven't yet
logged into (tty2-X, typically 6)?  are there lines referencing getty
in your /etc/inittab (assuming fedora still uses inittab)?  do you
have any commands in your .logout file?  do the system logs say
anything about the tty or processes associated with it, or in fact,
anything at all at time of logout?

> The problem I'm having is if I login from the local terminal, when I log
> out, the screen goes blank and I just see a single dash in the upper
> left corner and that terminal window is now hung. I can use the next one
> (Alt-F2) OK, but when I log out of that one, it hangs too.

Sounds like a problem with respawning.  Unfortunately, I don't have
FC9 installed.  However, this is what I tried using Ubuntu 8.04:

- loged in to tty1 then loged out
- loged in to tty2
- typed 'ps faux | grep -w tty[1-2]'

root     20801  0.0  0.0   6928  2604 tty2     Ss   11:24   0:00
/bin/login --
rwcitek  20832  0.0  0.0   5036  2404 tty2     S+   11:24   0:00  \_ -bash
root     20822  0.0  0.0   1716   508 tty1     Ss+  11:24   0:00
/sbin/getty 38400 tty1

- typed 'grep -w tty[1-2] /var/log/syslog | tail'

Jul 26 11:16:47 Ubuntu804 init: tty1 main process ended, respawning
Jul 26 11:17:14 Ubuntu804 init: tty2 main process ended, respawning
Jul 26 11:18:16 Ubuntu804 init: tty2 main process ended, respawning
Jul 26 11:18:17 Ubuntu804 init: tty2 main process ended, respawning
Jul 26 11:20:05 Ubuntu804 init: tty1 main process ended, respawning
Jul 26 11:24:30 Ubuntu804 init: tty2 main process ended, respawning
Jul 26 11:24:39 Ubuntu804 init: tty1 main process ended, respawning


There may be a similar method in FC9.  I would suspect that if tty1 is
not respawning it would show up in the process table and in the logs.

Regards,
Robert

password, with it already in the text box. I hit <enter> and it goes
away. Then, after a while, I get it again. A restart of T-bird sometimes
makes this go away.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Sat Jul 26 18:42:06 2008
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Sat, 26 Jul 2008 18:42:06 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] UDP packet level testing
Message-ID: <20080727014206.GA3289@gate.kl-ic.com>


I want to test for dropped UDP packets between two specific machines
over the internet.  I have root access to both machines.  I would
like to be able to control the destination port, packet size, etc. 
Burst testing would be nice but not mandatory.  What I DON'T want
to do is throw data at a kernel buffer or socket or whatever, and
let the kernel choose the packet size.

Are there any good tools for this?  I've tried nttcp, but that is
stream oriented, and seems to let the kernel choose packet sizes. 
iperf is an elaboration of nttcp, and nettest is a wrapper around
iperf.  Too high level, not enough instrumentation.

What this is all about is that I am told that my Actiontec cable
router to Verizon FIOS truncates UDP packets to 512 bytes.   I
would like to test that before I ask Verizon to switch me over
to direct Cat5 connection (ditching the feature-laden but poorly
implemented Actiontec).

BTW, is there any way to set the mtu (maximum package size) that
an interface/protocol will use FOR UDP ONLY, without hacking the
kernel or restricting TCP and other protocols?  I will want to
do this as a further test.  I know I can do "ifconfig eth1 mtu 500"
on the interface, to limit all packet sizes, but I would like to
try it on UDP only.

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

>
> I want to test for dropped UDP packets between two specific machines
> over the internet.  I have root access to both machines.  I would
> like to be able to control the destination port, packet size, etc.
> Burst testing would be nice but not mandatory.  What I DON'T want
> to do is throw data at a kernel buffer or socket or whatever, and
> let the kernel choose the packet size.
>
> Are there any good tools for this?  I've tried nttcp, but that is
> stream oriented, and seems to let the kernel choose packet sizes.
> iperf is an elaboration of nttcp, and nettest is a wrapper around
> iperf.  Too high level, not enough instrumentation.
>
> What this is all about is that I am told that my Actiontec cable
> router to Verizon FIOS truncates UDP packets to 512 bytes.   I
> would like to test that before I ask Verizon to switch me over
> to direct Cat5 connection (ditching the feature-laden but poorly
> implemented Actiontec).
>
> BTW, is there any way to set the mtu (maximum package size) that
> an interface/protocol will use FOR UDP ONLY, without hacking the
> kernel or restricting TCP and other protocols?  I will want to
> do this as a further test.  I know I can do "ifconfig eth1 mtu 500"
> on the interface, to limit all packet sizes, but I would like to
> try it on UDP only.
>
> Keith
>
> --
> Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Sat Jul 26 18:56:39 2008
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Sat, 26 Jul 2008 18:56:39 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] OSCON sign for PLUG general meeting
Message-ID: <20080727015639.GA3420@gate.kl-ic.com>


Before we left the OSCON exhibit area, I snagged the 5 foot long
booth sign that OSCON provided for PLUG, instead of discarding it.

If we put a sticker over the "615" booth number, we can hang it
up in the front window of the PSU engineering building during
our meetings to let people know where we are, visible from the
street.  We would need some way to temporarily attach the sign
inside the window that doesn't leave adhesive gunk.  The sign
is sturdy cardboard, and has two mounting holes that would work
with a wire and hooks.  If I recall correctly, the windows are
framed with aluminum channel, so two light C clamps on the
verticals, and some picture wire between them, would do the trick.

I might not always make it to the meetings, so if we do figure
out a way to use this sign, it might be better to put a regular
attendee in charge of it.  It will roll up into a one foot diameter
cylinder, any tighter and it will develop a permanent curve.

Ideas?
  
Keith

There is an observation deck at the OHSU hospital that has an amazing view
of the city from the top of the hill. You can either catch the tram from
downtown or hop a bus from SW Portland. Or you can walk up Sam Jackson Park
Road like I did the first time I went up there. Its quite a hike thought,
and there are no real sidewalks, if you fancy an adventure.

Robert Citek wrote:
> One thing I was hoping for was a good vista point to get a photo shot
> of Mt. St. Helens and Mt. Hood.  Any recommendations for next time?
>   
The lawn at Pittock Mansion has views of both mountains. The Wildwood
trail goes to Pittock Mansion from near the World Forestry Center in
Washington Park (across from the zoo).

Another view point, but not really walking distance from downtown, is
the stone structure on Rocky Butte (it's just west of I-205 and just
north of I-84). You can also see Mt. Adams, and probably Mt. Ranier from
there. I'm no expert with the Trimet route finder web page, but it looks
like the 33-Fremont line runs out to Rocky Butte Rd. You'll have to walk
up from there.

Of course, all of these depend on the weather.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens

at performance with this tool you may need to adjust the kernel buffer sizes.

On Sat, Jul 26, 2008 at 08:37:38PM -0700, wes wrote:
> I don't know that it will satisfy all of your requirements, but I have used
> netcat (or "nc") for many types of tests and experiments.

nc is an interesting tool, thanks for pointing it out.  However, it
does not seem to move packets per se, but instead messages of arbitrary
length.  tcpdump at the receive or transmit ends shows everything being
reformed into 1024 byte packets.  Fooey!

However, the fact that the 1024 byte UDP packets are moving shows that
the web page I was reading was wrong, and the Actiontec is not truncating
packets longer than 512 bytes.

More tools and investigation needed.

> In response to your question regarding the MTU: If it's just for testing,
> why bother making it UDP-only? I woudl just let it affect TCP for the time
> it takes to do the tests.

Partly because I need the longer TCP channel without fragmenting to 
monitor the test.  I think???

On Sat, Jul 26, 2008 at 09:38:23PM -0700, Robert Citek wrote:
> 
> One thing I was hoping for was a good vista point to get a photo shot
> of Mt. St. Helens and Mt. Hood.  Any recommendations for next time?

As I recall, you can get a pretty good view of Mt. Saint Helens from
45.5143, -122.7153 in Washington Park up the hill from the Zoo.
IIRC you can see both from the Pittock Mansion at 45.5254, -122.7155
but that is a much longer hike from the Zoo.  The hills are pretty
bumpy up there, and covered with trees, so it is hard to find
good places with 360 degree panoramas.  That's the way we like it.

Keep in mind that Mt. St. Helens is slightly east of north from
Portland, while Mt. Hood is slightly south of east.  A panorama
including both would be about 90 degrees.

Your best shot of both would probably be from the top of one of 
the taller buildings, or perhaps from the upper cable tram
terminal at OHSU.  

Perhaps we ought to move this to PLUG talk, unless somebody
has a plan to install a Linux controlled camera on one of
the TV antennas on the top of the West Hills, so Robert can
get his panorama ...

Keith

< > Packet Generator (USE WITH CAUTION)

This module will inject preconfigured packets, at a configurable
rate, out of a given interface.  It is used for network interface
stress testing and performance analysis.  If you don't understand
what was just said, you don't need it: say N.

Documentation on how to use the packet generator can be found at
<file:Documentation/networking/pktgen.txt>.

To compile this code as a module, choose M here: the module will
be called pktgen.

   Symbol: NET_PKTGEN [=n]
   Prompt: Packet Generator (USE WITH CAUTION)
     Defined at net/Kconfig:198
     Depends on: NET && PROC_FS
     Location:
       -> Networking
         -> Networking support (NET [=y])
           -> Networking options
             -> Network testing


This little guy is in the 2.6 kernel.  I never iused it, but it always
looked intriguing.

Carlos Konstanski

> Jul 26 11:18:16 Ubuntu804 init: tty2 main process ended, respawning
> Jul 26 11:18:17 Ubuntu804 init: tty2 main process ended, respawning

> Jul 26 11:24:30 Ubuntu804 init: tty2 main process ended, respawning
> Jul 26 11:24:39 Ubuntu804 init: tty1 main process ended, respawning
>

Galen> There's also Council Crest Park.


Best views (car accessible) in my opinion are:

  Mt St Helens:  Windy Ridge (lat/long: 46.250079,-122.137365) paved,
                 but newspaper said recently the road was closed at
                 beargrass meadows
  <http://maps.google.com/maps?f=q&hl=en&geocode=&q=46.250079,-122.137365&ie=UTF8&t=h&z=16&iwloc=addr>

  Mt Hood:  Cloud Cap Inn (lat/long: 45.404049,-121.654312) at the end
            of a ~10 mile dusty/washboardy road
  <http://maps.google.com/maps?f=q&hl=en&geocode=&q=45.404049,-121.654312&ie=UTF8&t=h&z=16&iwloc=addr>

Not in Portland, obviously, but stellar views.  Rocky Butte (already
mentioned) is the other in-town spot.  Nice views of the Columbia
River and the airport from there too.
